  28. I've read almost all of the negative reviews, and they show a misunderstanding of what to expect and of how to use this product. So I've divided this review into the following labeled sections:<br /> 1. MY PERSPECTIVE<br /> 2. WHAT TO EXPECT ON FIRST USE<br /> 3. HOW I SHAVE WITH CREMO CREAM<br /> 4. HOW LONG DOES A TUBE OF CREMO CREAM LAST?<br /><br />Let's get going...<br />1. MY PERSPECTIVE<br />This review is for both head shavers and others. I mention this only because those of us who shave our heads are especially cautious about our products. For example, I use two razors - a Gillette Sensor (cheaper) for my face and a Gillette Mach 3 (more expensive) for my head - because blades are crazy expensive but I feel the need to invest more in my scalp. Before I switched to Cremo I used Aveeno Positively Smooth Shave Gel exclusively for years. I still say it is the best shave gel and the only thing I would use if Cremo weren't available. A can of Positively Smooth costs about the same as a tube of Cremo Cream but it lasts perhaps 1/5th as long and isn't as good. If Cremo went out of business or changed its formula, I would switch back to Aveeno. I hope that never happens.<br /><br />2. WHAT TO EXPECT ON FIRST USE<br />See the next section for specifics on how I use Cremo. The package claims that it creates a light lather. I think that's a misleading statement. When you wet your skin and apply the cream in the appropriate proportion, you may see a little white cream on your skin at first, but it will be very little and will likely disappear very quickly. Don't worry - it's still there and will still protect you well. It is simply not made to create a lather. Expect more like what you'd experience with a skin conditioning cream or hand lotion.<br /><br />You'll also feel a sort of gritty texture at first. I'm not certain the purpose of this - maybe the grit contains some of the magic. But it doesn't stay like an exfoliator would. The grit disappears quickly too. Because the cream and grit disappear quickly, you'll need to switch your mindset from knowing where to shave by where there's still foam to knowing where to shave by where there's still stubble. It's an easy switch, and I've grown to prefer it this way.<br /><br />Finally, you will probably feel a little more &#34;drag&#34; against the stubble than you're used to. This actually took me the most to get used to. It doesn't hurt, it's just different from the feel of shaving with other products. I've realized that the upside of this is that you are getting a much closer shave.<br /><br />3. HOW I SHAVE WITH CREMO CREAM<br />Here's my method and the one I recommend to everyone. If you don't shave your head you can easily adapt it to your needs.<br /> a. I fill the sink with very hot water<br /> b. I wet my head and face with the water<br /> c. I squeeze an amount of Cremo into my hand that is only about the amount of toothpaste advertisers show on toothbrushes.<br /> d. I rub my hands together a little and rub it into the skin on my head and face in circular motions<br /> e. I re-wet my hands a little and pat fresh hot water on my head only<br /> f. I shave my head as normal (I ALWAYS shave against the growth) - I rinse my razor in the sink frequently<br /> g. I re-wet my hands and rub the water on my face to re-activate the Cremo that I put there before<br /> h. I shave my face (again, always against the growth, and again rinsing the razor frequently)<br /> i. When done I simply rub the remaining Cremo into my skin. It makes a nice conditioner too.<br /><br />4. HOW LONG DOES A TUBE OF CREMO CREAM LAST?<br />Much longer than the tube says! I am now on my 3rd tube of Cremo Cream. This time I decided to measure how long it lasts.<br /><br />First you should know that I have an extra-large head (XL hats don't fit me), I have a very coarse beard, and the hair on my head is somewhat coarse too. Both grow back enough to shave once per day, but to be economical I actually shave every 1.5 days (if I shave this morning, my next shave will be tomorrow night, etc.). I also shave the back of my neck once per week but I don't increase the amount of Cremo I use. The only thing I don't shave is a small goatee and so-called &#34;soul patch&#34; below my lower lip.<br /><br />I started using the current tube of Cremo Cream on July 4, 2014. Today is January 2, 2015 - 6 months later. I'm certain I still have enough in the tube for at least another month!<br />------------<br />EDIT<br />------------<br />My tube finally ran out today. It lasted for this headshaver from July 4, 2014 to March 3 2015, 8 months. You can't beat this for around $6-$7, and you get the best shave as well!lly shave every 1.5 days (if I shave this morning, my next shave will be tomorrow night, etc.).   258. Okay, this is for all those 1 star reviews that complained about the lack of lather.<br /><br />You need to read the tube...really. The makers state rather clearly that their problem with traditional shave cream is that too much of the product does nothing for you at all, due to too much lather.<br /><br />This product is designed to coat the skin in a thin lubricating layer *without much lather at all*. If you want mountains of white foamy shave cream on your face, you've got the wrong product!! it's not the maker's fault, however, as they have stated so in a very obvious fashion.<br /><br />So, forget everything you know about shave creams and gels for now and assume you've never shaved before. You only need a very small amount to cover your face. Again, the recommended amount is an 'almond-sized' amount, not a pile of stuff in your hand. If you use too much it will, as some have complained, gum up your razor. I've been using this stuff for almost a month now, and I use Gillette Fusion on my face and head. No gumming or clogging issues with my razor and this shave cream. I have also noticed it doesn't make a mess of my sink like other shave creams and gels have in the past.<br /><br />When you rub it into your face, or between your hands, it's not going to lather up much at all. Several years ago I grew tired of the ineffective shaving creams/gels and the wildly overpriced cartridge type blades so I went back to the basics, a nice quality DE89 razor, a badger brush, and a shaving bowl. Try this just once and you will be a fan, I promise. So here it is, I have my badger brush, Cremeo, and my good razor in the shower. To start, let the warm shower moisten your brush for a minute, just enough to get it saturated with water. Shake out the excess water with a flick of the wrist and add about and almond size dollop of Cremeo directly on your brush. Then whip up a nice lather by working your beard the brush, very quickly a nice lather will gather on your face. Once lathered, grab your razor and shave. The blade will slide across your face smoothly and effortlessly leaving behind a shave so smooth even your kids will notice. I use the 3 pass method most often, and trust me, the brush will hold enough lather for all three passes. Try this once, and I am convinced you will be a fan of this product, and of the Mud Method. ;-)

  303. I have used a lot of shave creams, gels, foams, etc. over the past two decades. Cremo's Shave Cream is (along with a Proraso cream I also use) THE BEST I have ever used. Simultaneously, it does not irritate my sensitive skin and it helps to prevent the skin on my face from drying out.<br /><br />I agree with other Reviewers who have noted that you need to prepare this cream correctly in order to get the maximum benefits, and it is very important to understand that this is a very concentrated product. Hotter water to the face prior to application makes shaving easier and makes this product work best (and it is worth noting that water that is hotter works better than water that is just warm). Then, a small size (I use about 2-3 peas worth) is what should be worked into the already wet skin on the face. REALLY work it in good and develop a nice lather that is neither runny nor so thick that it is difficult to rinse off of the razor. When you really work this cream into your skin, you are not just prepping for a close shave, but you are also massaging the moisturizers into your skin, and this WILL greatly reduce irritation. Now you are ready to shave.<br /><br />I shave using the Fusion Pro Glides as I find that reduces irritation over standard razors. I cannot tell you how well this works with other razors, but with the Pro Glide it works wonders. You can shave against the grain without irritation.
